Automatically classifies tasks into compliance tiers and enforces appropriate verification.\n\n**Key Benefits**:\n- Single command replaces confusion between `sc:task` and `sc:task-mcp`\n- Automatic tier classification with confidence scoring\n- Appropriate verification for each task type\n- Prevents over-engineering for trivial changes\n- Ensures safety for critical changes\n\n## Triggers\n\nUse `/sc:task` when:\n- Task involves code modifications with downstream impacts\n- Complexity score >0.6 with code modifications\n- Multi-file scope (>2 estimated affected files)\n- Security domain paths detected (auth/, security/, crypto/)\n- Refactoring or system-wide changes requested\n\n**Auto-Suggest Keywords**:\n- High confidence: \"implement feature\", \"refactor system\", \"fix security\", \"add authentication\", \"update database schema\"\n- Moderate confidence: \"add new\", \"create component\", \"update service\", \"modify API\"\n\n## Usage\n\n```bash\n/sc:task [description]                           # Auto-detect all dimensions\n/sc:task [description] --compliance strict       # Force STRICT tier\n/sc:task [description] --compliance light        # Force LIGHT tier\n/sc:task [description] --skip-compliance         # Bypass compliance (escape hatch)\n/sc:task [description] --verify auto             # Auto-select verification\n```\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\n### 0. Classification (Already Performed)\n\nClassification was handled by the `/sc:task` command before this skill was invoked. The tier has been determined and the classification header has been emitted. Proceed directly to execution based on the classified tier.\n\n**Reference** — the tier keyword tables (for context only, do not re-classify):\n- **STRICT**: security, authentication, database, migration, refactor, breaking change, encrypt, token, session, oauth\n- **EXEMPT**: explain, search, commit, push, plan, discuss, brainstorm\n- **LIGHT**: typo, comment, whitespace, lint, docstring, formatting, minor\n- **STANDARD**: implement, add, create, update, fix, build, modify, change (default)\n\n### 2. Confidence Display (Human-Readable)\n\nAfter the mandatory classification header, show a human-readable summary:\n\n```\n**Tier: STANDARD** [████████░░] 80%\n\nClassified as STANDARD:\n- Keywords matched: add, implement\n- Confidence score: 0.78\n- Considered alternatives: STRICT (0.35)\n```\n\nIf confidence <70%, add prompt: \"⚠️ Low confidence. Override with: `--compliance [strict|standard|light|exempt]`\"\n\n**Note**: The machine-readable header (Section 0) is for telemetry/A/B testing. This human-readable display is for user understanding.\n\n### 3. Execution Phase\n\nExecute task according to tier requirements:\n\n**STRICT Execution**:\n1. Activate project (mcp__serena__activate_project)\n2. Verify git working directory clean (git status)\n3. Load codebase context (codebase-retrieval)\n4. Check relevant memories (list_memories -> read_memory)\n5. Identify all affected files and test files\n6. Make changes with full checklist\n7. Identify all files that import changed code\n8. Update all affected files\n9. Spawn verification agent (quality-engineer)\n10. Run comprehensive tests: `pytest [path] -v`\n11. Answer adversarial questions\n\n**STANDARD Execution**:\n1. Load context via codebase-retrieval\n2. Search downstream impacts (find_referencing_symbols OR grep)\n3. Make changes\n4. Run affected tests OR document manual verification\n5. Verify basic functionality\n\n**LIGHT Execution**:\n1. Quick scope check (files/lines within bounds)\n2. Make changes\n3. Quick sanity check (syntax valid, no obvious errors)\n4. Proceed with judgment\n\n**EXEMPT Execution**:\n1. Execute immediately\n2. No verification overhead\n\n### 4. Verification Phase\n\nRoute to appropriate verification based on tier and paths:\n\n| Compliance Tier | Verification Method | Token Cost | Timeout |\n|-----------------|---------------------|------------|---------|\n| STRICT | Sub-agent (quality-engineer) | 3-5K | 60s |\n| STANDARD | Direct test execution | 300-500 | 30s |\n| LIGHT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n| EXEMPT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n\n**Critical Path Override**: Paths matching `auth/`, `security/`, `crypto/`, `models/`, `migrations/` always trigger CRITICAL verification regardless of compliance tier.\n\n**Trivial Path Override**: Paths matching `*.md`, `docs/`, `*test*.py` may skip verification.\n\n### 5. Feedback Collection\n\nAfter completion, collect implicit feedback:\n- Track if user overrode tier (implicit classification feedback)\n- Note smooth completion vs errors (quality signal)\n- Store for calibration learning\n\n## MCP Integration\n\n**Required Servers by Tier**:\n- STRICT: Sequential, Serena (fallback not allowed)\n- STANDARD: Sequential, Context7 (fallback allowed)\n- LIGHT: None required (fallback allowed)\n- EXEMPT: None required\n\n**Circuit Breaker Behavior**:\n- If required servers unavailable for STRICT tier, block task execution\n- For other tiers, use fallbacks with noted limitations\n\n## Tool Coordination\n\n**Planning Phase**:\n1. TodoWrite: Create task breakdown\n2. codebase-retrieval: Load context\n3. list_memories / read_memory: Check project state\n\n**Execution Phase**:\n1. Edit/MultiEdit/Write: Make changes\n2. Grep/Glob: Find references\n3. find_referencing_symbols: Trace dependencies\n\n**Verification Phase**:\n1. Task (quality-engineer): Spawn verification agent (STRICT only)\n2. Bash: Run tests directly (STANDARD)\n3. think_about_task_adherence: Reflect on completeness\n\n**Completion Phase**:\n1. write_memory: Save session state\n2. think_about_whether_you_are_done: Final check\n\n## Examples\n\n### STRICT Task\n```\n/sc:task \"implement user authentication with JWT\"\n\n-> Classified as STRICT (security domain, authentication keyword)\n-> Full 6-category checklist enforced\n-> Verification agent spawned\n-> Adversarial questions answered\n```\n\n### STANDARD Task\n```\n/sc:task \"add pagination to user list\"\n\n-> Classified as STANDARD (add keyword, typical feature)\n-> Context loaded before editing\n-> Downstream impacts checked\n-> Direct test execution\n```\n\n### LIGHT Task\n```\n/sc:task \"fix typo in README\"\n\n-> Classified as LIGHT (trivial pattern detected)\n-> Immediate execution\n-> No compliance overhead\n```\n\n### Override Example\n```\n/sc:task \"update config file\" --compliance strict\n\n-> User override to STRICT regardless of classification\n-> Full verification enforced\n```\n\n## Boundaries\n\n**Will:**\n- Classify tasks into appropriate compliance tiers\n- Enforce tier-appropriate verification requirements\n- Provide This represents analysis truth, not\n   249→    enforcement policy. Gate enforcement depends on rollout_mode -- see\n   250→    _zero_blocking_findings_for_mode(). Use blocking_for_mode() to determine\n   251→    whether findings would block under a given rollout mode.\n   252→    \"\"\"\n   253→\n   254→    target_dir: str\n   255→    files_analyzed: int = 0\n   256→    files_skipped: int = 0\n   257→    unwired_callables: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n   258→    orphan_modules: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n   259→    unwired_registries: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n   260→\n   261→    @property\n   262→    def total_findings(self) -> int:\n   263→        \"\"\"Single-source computation: category counts derive from list lengths.\"\"\"\n   264→        return (\n   265→            len(self.unwired_callables)\n   266→            + len(self.orphan_modules)\n   267→            + len(self.unwired_registries)\n   268→        )\n   269→\n   270→    @property\n   271→    def clean(self) -> bool:\n   272→        \"\"\"Returns True when analysis found zero issues.\n   273→\n   274→        This is analysis truth, not enforcement policy. Gate pass\n   275→        depends on rollout_mode via _zero_blocking_findings_for_mode().\n   276→        \"\"\"\n   277→        return self.total_findings == 0\n   278→\n   279→    def blocking_for_mode(self, mode: str) -> int:\n   280→        \"\"\"Return count of blocking findings for a given rollout mode.\n   281→\n   282→        - shadow: 0 (never blocks)\n   283→        - soft: critical_count only\n   284→        - full: critical_count + major_count\n   285→        \"\"\"\n   286→        all_findings = (\n   287→            self.unwired_callables + self.orphan_modules + self.unwired_registries\n   288→        )\n   289→        if mode == \"shadow\":\n   290→            return 0\n   291→        elif mode == \"soft\":\n   292→            return sum(1 for f in all_findings if f.severity == \"critical\")\n   293→        else:  # full\n   294→            return sum(\n   295→                1 for f in all_findings if f.severity in (\"critical\", \"major\")\n   296→            )\n   297→```\n   298→\n   299→<!-- Source: Invariant INV-008 — severity counts are derived properties from same finding lists -->\n   300→\n   301→**Single-source computation requirement**: Both category counts (`unwired_callable_count`, `orphan_module_count`, `unwired_registry_count`) and severity counts (`critical_count`, `major_count`, `info_count`) are computed by iterating the same typed finding lists. The `emit_report()` function derives both projections from `WiringReport`'s three lists, making the three-way invariant (`category_sum == severity_sum == total_findings`) a tautology. The semantic checks `_finding_counts_consistent` and `_severity_summary_consistent` validate the serialized form as a defense against report corruption or manual editing.\n   302→\n   303→<!-- Source: Debate X-006 / Refactor W-001 — renamed .passed to .clean, added blocking_for_mode() -->\n   304→<!-- Source: Debate A-008 consensus — added files_skipped field -->\n   305→\n   306→### 5.2 Analysis Functions\n   307→\n   308→#### 5.2.1 Unwired Callable Analysis\n   309→\n   310→**Purpose**: Detect constructor parameters typed `Optional[Callable]` (or `Callable | None`) with default `None` that are never explicitly provided at any call site.\n   311→\n   312→**Algorithm**:\n   313→\n   314→```\n   315→1. AST-parse all Python files in target directory\n   316→2. For each class __init__:\n   317→   a. Extract params where:\n   318→      - ast.unparse(annotation) matches \\bCallable\\b pattern\n   319→      - default is ast.Constant with value None\n   320→   b. Record: (class_name, param_name, file_path, line)\n   321→3. For each injectable:\n   322→   a. Search all Python files for call sites constructing that class\n   323→   b. Check if any call site provides the parameter by keyword\n   324→   c. Zero providers -> WiringFinding(unwired_callable)\n   325→```\n   326→\n   327→**Pattern matched** (from forensic report):\n   328→```python\n   329→class PortifyExecutor:\n   330→    def __init__(self, ..., step_runner: Optional[Callable] = None):\n   331→        ...\n   332→\n   333→# This call does NOT provide step_runner:\n   334→executor = PortifyExecutor(steps=steps, workdir=workdir, ...)\n   335→# -> Finding: unwired_callable, PortifyExecutor.step_runner\n   336→```\n   337→\n   338→**Whitelist**: `wiring_whitelist.yaml` with schema:\n   339→```yaml\n   340→unwired_callables:\n   341→  - symbol: \"module.path.ClassName.param_name\"\n   342→    reason: \"Intentional event hook\"\n   343→```\n   344→\n   345→Validation: entries missing `symbol` or `reason` are MALFORMED. In Phase 1 (shadow), malformed entries are logged as WARNING and skipped. In Phase 2+, malformed entries raise `WiringConfigError`.\n   346→\n   347→**Known limitation (v2.0)**: Import aliases and re-exports not resolved. Expected 30-70% FPR contribution. Planned fix in v2.1: alias pre-pass via `ast.Import`/`ast.ImportFrom` traversal with `__init__.py` chain resolution (max 3 hops).\n   348→\n   349→**Severity policy**:\n   350→- **critical**: execution/dispatch/enforcement behavior depends on the seam\n   351→- **major**: seam is dead but local fallback exists\n   352→- **info**: whitelisted intentional optional\n   353→\n   354→#### 5.2.2 Orphan Module Analysis\n   355→\n   356→**Purpose**: Detect Python files in provider directories whose exported functions are never imported by any consumer.\n   357→\n   358→**Algorithm**:\n   359→\n   360→```\n   361→1. Identify provider directories by convention:\n   362→   - names matching config.provider_dir_names\n   363→   - directories containing 3+ Python files with common function prefix\n   364→2. For each Python file in provider directory:\n   365→   a. AST-parse, extract top-level def (excluding _private)\n   366→   b. Search all Python files OUTSIDE provider dir for imports\n   367→   c. Zero importers -> WiringFinding(orphan_module)\n   368→```\n   369→\n   370→**Pattern matched**:\n   371→```python\n   372→# src/superclaude/cli/cli_portify/steps/validate_config.py\n   373→def run_validate_config():  # never imported by executor.py\n   374→    ...\n   375→# -> Finding: orphan_module, steps/validate_config.py::run_validate_config\n   376→```\n   377→\n   378→**Exclusions**: `__init__.py`, `conftest.py`, `test_*.py`\n   379→\n   380→**Evidence rule**: A symbol is orphaned only if BOTH:\n   381→1. Direct analysis finds no effective import/call chain\n   382→2. Cleanup-audit evidence does not justify dynamic or deferred use\n   383→\n   384→#### 5.2.3 Unwired Registry Analysis\n   385→\n   386→**Purpose**: Detect dispatch registry dictionaries whose values reference non-importable functions.\n   387→\n   388→**Algorithm**:\n   389→\n   390→```\n   391→1. AST-parse all Python files\n   392→2. For each module-level assignment where:\n   393→   a. Target name matches REGISTRY_PATTERNS\n   394→   b. Value is a Dict literal\n   395→3. For each dict entry:\n   396→   a. If value is Name node: verify importable in scope\n   397→   b. If value is string: verify resolves to module.function\n   398→   c. If value is None: flag as explicit null handler\n   399→4. Unresolvable -> WiringFinding(unwired_registry)\n   400→```\n   401→\n   402→**Registry patterns** (configurable):\n   403→```python\n   404→DEFAULT_REGISTRY_PATTERNS = re.compile(\n   405→    r\"^(STEP_REGISTRY|STEP_DISPATCH|PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS|\"\n   406→    r\"\\w*_REGISTRY|\\w*_DISPATCH|\\w*_HANDLERS|\\w*_ROUTER|\\w*_BUILDERS)$\"\n   407→)\n   408→```\n   409→\n   410→Three detection classes:\n   411→1. **entry unresolved** -- mapped target does not resolve -> critical\n   412→2. **registry unused** -- registry or accessor has zero external consumers -> major\n   413→3. **explicit None** -- entry maps to None with no alternate handler -> major\n   414→\n   415→### 5.3 ToolOrchestrator AST Analyzer Plugin\n   416→\n   417→```python\n   418→# src/superclaude/cli/audit/wiring_analyzer.py\n   419→\n   420→from __future__ import annotations\n   421→\n   422→import ast\n   423→from pathlib import Path\n   424→\n   425→from .tool_orchestrator import FileAnalysis\n   426→\n   427→\n   428→def ast_analyze_file(file_path: Path, content: str) -> FileAnalysis:\n   429→    \"\"\"AST-based file analyzer for ToolOrchestrator injection.\n   430→\n   431→    Populates the `references` field that the default line-based\n   432→    analyzer leaves empty.\n   433→\n   434→    Usage: ToolOrchestrator(analyzer=ast_analyze_file)\n   435→    \"\"\"\n   436→    try:\n   437→        tree = ast.parse(content, filename=str(file_path))\n   438→    except SyntaxError:\n   439→        return FileAnalysis(\n   440→            imports=[], exports=[], references=[], metadata={}\n   441→        )\n   442→\n   443→    imports = _extract_imports(tree)\n   444→    exports = _extract_exports(tree)\n   445→    references = _extract_references(tree, file_path)\n   446→\n   447→    return FileAnalysis(\n   448→        imports=imports,\n   449→        exports=exports,\n   450→        references=references,\n   451→        metadata={\n   452→            \"has_dispatch_registry\": _has_registry(tree),\n   453→            \"injectable_callables\": _count_injectable_callables(tree),\n   454→        },\n   455→    )\n   456→```\n   457→\n   458→**Integration**: Pass as `analyzer` parameter to `ToolOrchestrator.__init__()`. This populates the empty `references` field, improving:\n   459→- `dependency_graph.py` Tier-A edges (actual imports vs line-based)\n   460→- `dead_code.py` detection (symbol-level vs file-level)\n   461→- `profile_generator.py` coupling metric (real deps vs stem-matching)\n   462→\n   463→<!-- Source: Debate risk #2 / Refactor W-002 — ToolOrchestrator cut criteria -->\n   464→#### 5.3.1 Cut Criteria\n   465→\n   466→If T06 (ToolOrchestrator AST plugin) is not complete by the time T08 (roadmap integration) begins, defer T06 to v2.1. Core wiring gate functionality (T01-T05, T07-T10) does not depend on the ToolOrchestrator plugin. The cleanup-audit integration (Mode C) operates with reduced accuracy but still functions using line-based analysis.\n   467→\n   468→### 5.4 Report Format\n   469→\n   470→YAML frontmatter + Markdown body, conforming to `GateCriteria` validation:\n   471→\n   472→```yaml\n   473→---\n   474→gate: wiring-verification\n   475→target_dir: src/superclaude/cli/cli_portify\n   476→files_analyzed: 14\n   477→files_skipped: 0\n   478→rollout_mode: shadow\n   479→analysis_complete: true\n   480→audit_artifacts_used: 0\n   481→unwired_callable_count: 1\n   482→orphan_module_count: 2\n   483→unwired_registry_count: 0\n   484→critical_count: 3\n   485→major_count: 0\n   486→info_count: 0\n   487→total_findings: 3\n   488→blocking_findings: 3\n   489→whitelist_entries_applied: 0"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_011MgHGDgifxdH4Hhoo6F4hF","session_id":"f7cfd6cf-7532-40b9-8d40-effa914f33bb","uuid":"35dc20ce-6091-433d-99d1-f18d1dcda101","timestamp":"2026-03-19T04:27:13.136Z"}

Each adopts the proposed default from the roadmap Phase 0 table unless noted. Rationale references the source architect (Opus/Haiku/Both) and validates against the zero-pipeline-modification constraint.\n    14→\n    15→---\n    16→\n    17→## OQ-1: How are `audit_artifacts_used` located/counted?\n    18→\n    19→**Question**: When the wiring analyzer optionally consumes cleanup-audit evidence as a false-positive suppressor (Section 6.6 authority rule), how does it discover and count those artifacts?\n    20→\n    21→**Committed Answer**: Glob for `*-audit-report.yaml` in the output directory. The count of matched files is recorded as `audit_artifacts_used` in report frontmatter.\n    22→\n    23→**Rationale**: Glob-based discovery is deterministic and convention-aligned with existing audit output naming. No configuration needed — the output directory is already known from the pipeline context. If no audit artifacts exist, `audit_artifacts_used = 0` and the analyzer operates purely on direct AST analysis, which is the authoritative mode per Section 6.6.\n    24→\n    25→**Source**: Opus\n    26→\n    27→**Pipeline constraint check**: No pipeline substrate touched. The glob runs against output artifacts, not pipeline internals.\n    28→\n    29→---\n    30→\n    31→## OQ-2: Are `exclude_patterns` matches counted in `files_skipped`?\n    32→\n    33→**Question**: When `WiringConfig.exclude_patterns` (e.g., `test_*.py`, `conftest.py`, `__init__.py`) causes files to be excluded from analysis, are those files counted in the `files_skipped` frontmatter field?\n    34→\n    35→**Committed Answer**: Yes. Files matching `exclude_patterns` increment `files_skipped` for visibility. This means `files_analyzed + files_skipped` equals the total Python files discovered in `target_dir`.\n    36→\n    37→**Rationale**: Counting excluded files in `files_skipped` provides transparency about analysis scope. An operator reviewing the report can see exactly how many files were considered vs. analyzed. This supports the auditability design constraint (\"every enforcement decision must be explainable from report frontmatter and evidence sections alone\"). The alternative — silently excluding files — would make scope gaps invisible.\n    38→\n    39→**Source**: Opus\n    40→\n    41→**Pipeline constraint check**: No pipeline changes. `files_skipped` is a frontmatter field in the emitted report, validated by `WIRING_GATE.required_frontmatter_fields` which is defined in `audit/wiring_gate.py`.\n    42→\n    43→---\n    44→\n    45→## OQ-3: Is whitelist strictness derived from `rollout_mode`?\n    46→\n    47→**Question**: How strictly should malformed whitelist entries (missing `symbol` or `reason` fields) be handled? Should strictness vary by rollout mode?\n    48→\n    49→**Committed Answer**: Yes, strictness is mode-dependent:\n    50→- **shadow**: Malformed entries are logged as WARNING and skipped. Analysis continues.\n    51→- **soft/full**: Malformed entries raise `WiringConfigError`, halting analysis.\n    52→\n    53→**Rationale**: During shadow mode, the gate is non-blocking and the priority is data collection. Halting on a malformed whitelist entry would prevent shadow data gathering for no enforcement benefit. Once the gate is in soft or full mode, enforcement decisions depend on whitelist correctness — a malformed entry could silently suppress a real finding, so strict validation is warranted. This graduated approach matches the three-phase rollout philosophy.\n    54→\n    55→**Source**: Opus\n    56→\n    57→**Pipeline constraint check**: No pipeline changes. `WiringConfigError` is raised in `audit/wiring_config.py`. Whitelist loading is entirely within the new `audit/` modules.\n    58→\n    59→**Interaction note**: This decision interacts with OQ-5 (comparator/consolidator scope) only at the behavioral level — both are additive. No technical coupling.\n    60→\n    61→---\n    62→\n    63→## OQ-4: Does `SprintConfig.source_dir` already exist?\n    64→\n    65→**Question**: The sprint integration (Section 5.8) calls `run_wiring_analysis(target_dir=config.source_dir)`. Does `SprintConfig` already have a `source_dir` field, or does one need to be added?\n    66→\n    67→**Committed Answer**: Verify before Phase 3b implementation. If `source_dir` does not exist on `SprintConfig`, add it as part of Phase 3b task 3b.1 alongside the `wiring_gate_mode` field addition.\n    68→\n    69→**Rationale**: This is a factual question requiring code inspection at implementation time. Should they be restructured to handle wiring data natively?\n    80→\n    81→**Committed Answer**: Additive wiring sections only, no restructure. Specifically:\n    82→- **audit-comparator**: Add a cross-file wiring consistency check (Section 6.1, Table row 4).\n    83→- **audit-consolidator**: Add a \"Wiring Health\" section to the final report (Section 6.1, Table row 5).\n    84→\n    85→No existing agent tools change. How does `grace_period` interact with shadow mode?\n    98→\n    99→**Committed Answer**: Single accountable owner for shadow metrics and activation decisions. The owner is responsible for:\n   100→1. Monitoring shadow findings across release cycles (Phase 6a tasks 6a.1-6a.5)\n   101→2. Computing FPR/TPR/latency statistics\n   102→3. Producing the readiness report with explicit recommendation (Phase 6a task 6a.6)\n   103→4. Making the soft-mode and full-mode activation decisions (Phase 6b)\n   104→\n   105→**`grace_period` interaction** (from Section 7, Phase 1 operational note): Roadmap configurations should set `grace_period > 0` during shadow rollout to enable `GateMode.TRAILING` behavior via `TrailingGateRunner`. If `grace_period = 0` forces BLOCKING, shadow mode still passes because `_zero_blocking_findings_for_mode` reads `rollout_mode=shadow` from frontmatter and returns True unconditionally, and the emitter sets `blocking_findings=0` in shadow mode. However, TRAILING mode provides cleaner operational semantics.\n   106→\n   107→**Rationale**: Shadow-to-soft activation requires statistical judgment (FPR calibration formula: `measured_FPR + 2σ < 15%`). Distributing this across multiple people risks diffusion of responsibility and premature activation. A single owner can hold the line on \"Phase 2 MUST NOT activate if unwired-callable FPR cannot be separated from noise\" (Section 7 Phase 2).\n   108→\n   109→**Source**: Haiku\n   110→\n   111→**Pipeline constraint check**: `grace_period` is read from existing pipeline configuration, not modified. `TrailingGateRunner` is consumed as-is. No pipeline substrate changes.\n   112→\n   113→---\n   114→\n   115→## OQ-7: Merge sequencing with concurrent PRs?\n   116→\n   117→**Question**: How should merge sequencing be handled given that `roadmap/gates.py` is a shared modification point with concurrent PRs (e.g., Anti-Instincts `ANTI_INSTINCT_GATE` in v3.05, Unified Audit Gating `SPEC_FIDELITY_GATE` extensions)?\n   118→\n   119→**Committed Answer**: Complete Phases 1-2 before touching shared files. Specifically:\n   120→- Phases 1-2 create new files only (`audit/wiring_gate.py`, `audit/wiring_config.py`, `audit/wiring_analyzer.py`, test files) — no merge conflict risk.\n   121→- Phase 3a modifies `roadmap/executor.py`, `roadmap/gates.py`, and `roadmap/prompts.py` — these are the shared-file touchpoints requiring coordination.\n   122→- Preferred: single coordinated PR or sequenced PRs with explicit rebase points (Section 15).\n   123→\n   124→**Rationale**: Phases 1-2 represent ~70% of the implementation work and touch zero shared files. category sum == severity sum == total findings\n\nThat means report-frontmatter counters are derived views, not stored independent state.\n\n### Section 5.2.1 — Unwired Callable Analysis\nPurpose:\n- detect constructor parameters typed as `Optional[Callable]` or `Callable | None` with default `None`\n- report when no call site explicitly provides that parameter\n\nAlgorithm:\n1. parse all Python files in target directory with AST\n2. inspect each class `__init__`\n3. identify injectable params where:\n   - annotation matches Callable\n   - default is `None`\n4. for each injectable:\n   - search all Python files for constructor call sites\n   - check whether parameter is ever supplied by keyword\n   - if zero providers, emit `unwired_callable`\n\nWhitelist schema:\n- `wiring_whitelist.yaml`\n- shape:\n  - `unwired_callables`\n  - entries with `symbol` and `reason`\n\nMalformed whitelist behavior:\n- Phase 1 / shadow: warn and skip malformed entries\n- Phase 2+: raise `WiringConfigError`\n\nKnown limitation called out by spec:\n- aliases and re-exports are not resolved in v2.0\n- expected false-positive contribution: 30–70%\n- future fix planned via alias pre-pass and `__init__.py` chain resolution\n\nSeverity policy:\n- `critical`: dispatch/execution/enforcement depends on seam\n- `major`: local fallback exists\n- `info`: whitelisted intentional optional\n\n### Section 5.2.2 — Orphan Module Analysis\nPurpose:\n- detect Python files in provider directories whose exported functions are never imported by any consumer\n\nAlgorithm:\n1. identify provider directories by convention:\n   - names from `config.provider_dir_names`\n   - or directories containing 3+ Python files with a common function prefix\n2. for each Python file in provider dir:\n   - parse AST\n   - extract top-level non-private defs\n   - search all Python files outside provider dir for imports\n   - if zero importers, emit `orphan_module`\n\nExclusions:\n- `__init__.py`\n- `conftest.py`\n- `test_*.py`\n\nEvidence rule:\nA symbol is orphaned only if both are true:\n1. direct analysis finds no effective import/call chain\n2. cleanup-audit evidence does not justify dynamic or deferred use\n\nThat second clause matters a lot. This analysis is not purely static-AST; it can be suppressed by audit evidence.\n\n### Section 5.2.3 — Unwired Registry Analysis\nPurpose:\n- detect registry dictionaries whose values reference non-importable functions\n\nAlgorithm:\n1. parse all Python files with AST\n2. inspect module-level assignments where:\n   - target matches registry pattern regex\n   - value is a dict literal\n3. inspect each dict entry:\n   - `Name` node -> verify importable in scope\n   - string -> resolve to `module.function`\n   - `None` -> explicit null handler\n4. unresolved cases emit `unwired_registry`\n\nDefault registry regex:\n- matches names like:\n  - `STEP_REGISTRY`\n  - `STEP_DISPATCH`\n  - `PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS`\n  - `*_REGISTRY`\n  - `*_DISPATCH`\n  - `*_HANDLERS`\n  - `*_ROUTER`\n  - `*_BUILDERS`\n\nDetection classes and severities:\n1. entry unresolved -> `critical`\n2. registry unused / accessor has zero external consumers -> `major`\n3. explicit `None` with no alternate handler -> `major`\n\n### Section 5.3 — ToolOrchestrator AST Analyzer Plugin\nThis section defines an AST-based analyzer plugin expected at:\n- `src/superclaude/cli/audit/wiring_analyzer.py`\n\nIntended function:\n- `ast_analyze_file(file_path: Path, content: str) -> FileAnalysis`\n\nPurpose:\n- provide a better analyzer for `ToolOrchestrator`\n- populate `references`, which current default analyzer leaves empty\n\nIntegration model:\n- pass it as `analyzer` to `ToolOrchestrator(...)`\n\nIntended benefits:\n- improve `dependency_graph.py`\n- improve `dead_code.py`\n- improve `profile_generator.py`\n\nImportant current-code alignment:\n- the current `ToolOrchestrator` already accepts an injectable analyzer\n- the default analyzer is line-based\n- `references=[]` today\n- so this plugin design matches the existing extension point very cleanly\n\nCut criteria in 5.3.1:\n- if AST plugin slips, it can be deferred to v2.1\n- core wiring gate does not depend on it\n\nThat means the wiring gate and the ToolOrchestrator plugin are intentionally separable workstreams.\n\n## 6. files_analyzed: Number of Python files successfully parsed.\n        files_skipped: Number of files excluded or unparseable (OQ-2).\n        unwired_callables: Findings from unwired callable analysis (G-001).\n        orphan_modules: Findings from orphan module analysis (G-002).\n        unwired_registries: Findings from registry analysis (G-003).\n        scan_duration_seconds: Wall-clock time of analysis run.\n        rollout_mode: Active rollout mode for blocking semantics.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    target_dir: str = \"\"\n    files_analyzed: int = 0\n    files_skipped: int = 0\n    unwired_callables: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n    orphan_modules: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n    unwired_registries: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n    scan_duration_seconds: float = 0.0\n    rollout_mode: str = \"shadow\"\n\n    @property\n    def all_findings(self) -> list[WiringFinding]:\n        \"\"\"All findings across all categories.\"\"\"\n        return self.unwired_callables + self.orphan_modules + self.unwired_registries\n\n    @property\n    def total_findings(self) -> int:\n        \"\"\"Total finding count (category sum invariant).\"\"\"\n        return len(self.all_findings)\n\n    @property\n    def unsuppressed_findings(self) -> list[WiringFinding]:\n        \"\"\"Findings not suppressed by whitelist.\"\"\"\n        return [f for f in self.all_findings if not f.suppressed]\n\n    @property\n    def clean(self) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"True if zero unsuppressed findings regardless of rollout mode.\"\"\"\n        return len(self.unsuppressed_findings) == 0\n\n    def blocking_count(self, mode: str | None = None) -> int:\n        \"\"\"Count of findings that block the gate for the given rollout mode.\n\n        Args:\n            mode: Override rollout mode. Uses self.rollout_mode if None.\n\n        Returns:\n            Number of blocking findings per OQ-6:\n            - shadow: 0 (never blocks)\n            - soft: critical unsuppressed only\n            - full: critical + major unsuppressed\n        \"\"\"\n        effective_mode = mode or self.rollout_mode\n        unsuppressed = self.unsuppressed_findings\n\n        if effective_mode == \"shadow\":\n            return 0\n        elif effective_mode == \"soft\":\n            return sum(1 for f in unsuppressed if f.severity == \"critical\")\n        else:  # full\n            return sum(\n                1 for f in unsuppressed if f.severity in (\"critical\", \"major\")\n            )\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Analyzers (sections 5.2.1, 5.2.2, 5.2.3)\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n\ndef _collect_python_files(\n    source_dir: Path,\n    exclude_patterns: list[str],\n) -> tuple[list[Path], int]:\n    \"\"\"Collect Python files from source_dir, applying exclude patterns.\n\n    Returns:\n        Tuple of (included files, skipped count).\n    \"\"\"\n    included: list[Path] = []\n    skipped = 0\n\n    for py_file in sorted(source_dir.rglob(\"*.py\")):\n        name = py_file.name\n        if any(fnmatch(name, pat) for pat in exclude_patterns):\n            skipped += 1\n            continue\n        included.append(py_file)\n\n    return included, skipped\n\n\ndef _safe_parse(file_path: Path) -> ast.Module | None:\n    \"\"\"Parse a Python file, returning None on SyntaxError (R2 mitigation).\"\"\"\n    try:\n        source = file_path.read_text(encoding=\"utf-8\")\n        return ast.parse(source, filename=str(file_path))\n    except SyntaxError as exc:\n        logger.warning(\"SyntaxError parsing %s: %s — skipping\", file_path, exc)\n        return None\n    except (OSError, UnicodeDecodeError) as exc:\n        logger.warning(\"Cannot read %s: %s — skipping\", file_path, exc)\n        return None\n\n\ndef _apply_whitelist(\n    findings: list[WiringFinding],\n    whitelist: list[WhitelistEntry],\n) -> list[WiringFinding]:\n    \"\"\"Mark findings as suppressed if they match a whitelist entry.\"\"\"\n    suppressed_symbols = {\n        (e.symbol, e.finding_type) for e in whitelist\n    }\n    for finding in findings:\n        if (finding.symbol_name, finding.finding_type) in suppressed_symbols:\n            finding.suppressed = True\n            finding.severity = \"info\"\n    return findings\n\n\n# --- G-001: Unwired Callable Analysis (section 5.2.1) ---\n\n\ndef _extract_injectable_params(\n    tree: ast.Module, file_path: str\n) -> list[tuple[str, str, int]]:\n    \"\"\"Extract Optional[Callable] constructor parameters.\n\n    Returns list of (class_name.param_name, param_name, line_number).\n    \"\"\"\n    injectables: list[tuple[str, str, int]] = []\n\n    for node in ast.walk(tree):\n        if not isinstance(node, ast.ClassDef):\n            continue\n\n        for item in node.body:\n            if not isinstance(item, ast.FunctionDef) or item.name != \"__init__\":\n                continue\n\n            for arg in item.args.args:\n                if arg.arg == \"self\":\n                    continue\n                annotation = arg.annotation\n                if annotation is None:\n                    continue\n\n                # Check for Optional[Callable] or Callable | None\n                if _is_optional_callable(annotation):\n                    # Verify default is None\n                    if _has_none_default(item, arg):\n                        symbol = f\"{node.name}.{arg.arg}\"\n                        injectables.append(\n                            (symbol, arg.arg, arg.lineno)\n                        )\n\n    return injectables\n\n\ndef _is_optional_callable(annotation: ast.expr) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Check if an annotation represents Optional[Callable] or Callable | None.\"\"\"\n    # Optional[Callable] -> Subscript(Name('Optional'), Name('Callable'))\n    if isinstance(annotation, ast.Subscript):\n        if isinstance(annotation.value, ast.Name) and annotation.value.id == \"Optional\":\n            slice_val = annotation.slice\n            if isinstance(slice_val, ast.Name) and slice_val.id == \"Callable\":\n                return True\n            # Optional[Callable[...]]\n            if isinstance(slice_val, ast.Subscript):\n                if isinstance(slice_val.value, ast.Name) and slice_val.value.id == \"Callable\":\n                    return True\n        # Also check Attribute form: typing.Optional\n        if isinstance(annotation.value, ast.Attribute):\n            if annotation.value.attr == \"Optional\":\n                slice_val = annotation.slice\n                if isinstance(slice_val, ast.Name) and slice_val.id == \"Callable\":\n                    return True\n\n    # Callable | None -> BinOp(Name('Callable'), BitOr, Constant(None))\n    if isinstance(annotation, ast.BinOp) and isinstance(annotation.op, ast.BitOr):\n        left, right = annotation.left, annotation.right\n        if (isinstance(left, ast.Name) and left.id == \"Callable\" and\n                isinstance(right, ast.Constant) and right.value is None):\n            return True\n        if (isinstance(right, ast.Name) and right.id == \"Callable\" and\n                isinstance(left, ast.Constant) and left.value is None):\n            return True\n\n    return False\n\n\ndef _has_none_default(func_def: ast.FunctionDef, target_arg: ast.arg) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Check if the given arg has a default value of None.\"\"\"\n    args = func_def.args\n    # defaults apply to the last N positional args\n    all_args = args.args\n    defaults = args.defaults\n\n    if not defaults:\n        return False\n\n    # Map defaults to args (right-aligned)\n    offset = len(all_args) - len(defaults)\n    for i, arg in enumerate(all_args):\n        if arg is target_arg:\n            default_idx = i - offset\n            if 0 <= default_idx < len(defaults):\n                default = defaults[default_idx]\n                return isinstance(default, ast.Constant) and default.value is None\n    return False\n\n\ndef _find_wiring_call_sites(\n    param_name: str,\n    class_name: str,\n    trees: dict[Path, ast.Module],\n) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Search for call sites that explicitly provide the parameter by keyword.\"\"\"\n    for tree in trees.values():\n        for node in ast.walk(tree):\n            if isinstance(node, ast.Call):\n                # Check keyword arguments\n                for kw in node.keywords:\n                    if kw.arg == param_name:\n                        # Verify it's calling the right class\n                        if _is_class_call(node, class_name):\n                            return True\n    return False\n\n\ndef _is_class_call(call: ast.Call, class_name: str) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Check if a Call node is calling the specified class.\"\"\"\n    func = call.func\n    if isinstance(func, ast.Name) and func.id == class_name:\n        return True\n    if isinstance(func, ast.Attribute) and func.attr == class_name:\n        return True\n    return False\n\n\ndef analyze_unwired_callables(\n    config: WiringConfig,\n    source_dir: Path,\n) -> list[WiringFinding]:\n    \"\"\"Detect injectable callables (Optional[Callable]) that are never wired.\n\n    Algorithm (section 5.2.1):\n    1. Parse all Python files, extract Optional[Callable] constructor params\n    2. For each injectable, search all files for keyword call sites\n    3.    - full: critical + major unsuppressed\n        \"\"\"\n        effective_mode = mode or self.rollout_mode\n        unsuppressed = self.unsuppressed_findings\n\n        if effective_mode == \"shadow\":\n            return 0\n        elif effective_mode == \"soft\":\n            return sum(1 for f in unsuppressed if f.severity == \"critical\")\n        else:  # full\n            return sum(\n                1 for f in unsuppressed if f.severity in (\"critical\", \"major\")\n            )\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Analyzers (sections 5.2.1, 5.2.2, 5.2.3)\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n\ndef _collect_python_files(\n    source_dir: Path,\n    exclude_patterns: list[str],\n) -> tuple[list[Path], int]:\n    \"\"\"Collect Python files from source_dir, applying exclude patterns.\n\n    Returns:\n        Tuple of (included files, skipped count).\n    \"\"\"\n    included: list[Path] = []\n    skipped = 0\n\n    for py_file in sorted(source_dir.rglob(\"*.py\")):\n        name = py_file.name\n        if any(fnmatch(name, pat) for pat in exclude_patterns):\n            skipped += 1\n            continue\n        included.append(py_file)\n\n    return included, skipped\n\n\ndef _safe_parse(file_path: Path) -> ast.Module | None:\n    \"\"\"Parse a Python file, returning None on SyntaxError (R2 mitigation).\"\"\"\n    try:\n        source = file_path.read_text(encoding=\"utf-8\")\n        return ast.parse(source, filename=str(file_path))\n    except SyntaxError as exc:\n        logger.warning(\"SyntaxError parsing %s: %s — skipping\", file_path, exc)\n        return None\n    except (OSError, UnicodeDecodeError) as exc:\n        logger.warning(\"Cannot read %s: %s — skipping\", file_path, exc)\n        return None\n\n\ndef _apply_whitelist(\n    findings: list[WiringFinding],\n    whitelist: list[WhitelistEntry],\n) -> list[WiringFinding]:\n    \"\"\"Mark findings as suppressed if they match a whitelist entry.\"\"\"\n    suppressed_symbols = {\n        (e.symbol, e.finding_type) for e in whitelist\n    }\n    for finding in findings:\n        if (finding.symbol_name, finding.finding_type) in suppressed_symbols:\n            finding.suppressed = True\n            finding.severity = \"info\"\n    return findings\n\n\n# --- G-001: Unwired Callable Analysis (section 5.2.1) ---\n\n\ndef _extract_injectable_params(\n    tree: ast.Module, file_path: str\n) -> list[tuple[str, str, int]]:\n    \"\"\"Extract Optional[Callable] constructor parameters.\n\n    Returns list of (class_name.param_name, param_name, line_number).\n    \"\"\"\n    injectables: list[tuple[str, str, int]] = []\n\n    for node in ast.walk(tree):\n        if not isinstance(node, ast.ClassDef):\n            continue\n\n        for item in node.body:\n            if not isinstance(item, ast.FunctionDef) or item.name != \"__init__\":\n                continue\n\n            for arg in item.args.args:\n                if arg.arg == \"self\":\n                    continue\n                annotation = arg.annotation\n                if annotation is None:\n                    continue\n\n                # Check for Optional[Callable] or Callable | None\n                if _is_optional_callable(annotation):\n                    # Verify default is None\n                    if _has_none_default(item, arg):\n                        symbol = f\"{node.name}.{arg.arg}\"\n                        injectables.append(\n                            (symbol, arg.arg, arg.lineno)\n                        )\n\n    return injectables\n\n\ndef _is_optional_callable(annotation: ast.expr) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Check if an annotation represents Optional[Callable] or Callable | None.\"\"\"\n    # Optional[Callable] -> Subscript(Name('Optional'), Name('Callable'))\n    if isinstance(annotation, ast.Subscript):\n        if isinstance(annotation.value, ast.Name) and annotation.value.id == \"Optional\":\n            slice_val = annotation.slice\n            if isinstance(slice_val, ast.Name) and slice_val.id == \"Callable\":\n                return True\n            # Optional[Callable[...]]\n            if isinstance(slice_val, ast.Subscript):\n                if isinstance(slice_val.value, ast.Name) and slice_val.value.id == \"Callable\":\n                    return True\n        # Also check Attribute form: typing.Optional\n        if isinstance(annotation.value, ast.Attribute):\n            if annotation.value.attr == \"Optional\":\n                slice_val = annotation.slice\n                if isinstance(slice_val, ast.Name) and slice_val.id == \"Callable\":\n                    return True\n\n    # Callable | None -> BinOp(Name('Callable'), BitOr, Constant(None))\n    if isinstance(annotation, ast.BinOp) and isinstance(annotation.op, ast.BitOr):\n        left, right = annotation.left, annotation.right\n        if (isinstance(left, ast.Name) and left.id == \"Callable\" and\n                isinstance(right, ast.Constant) and right.value is None):\n            return True\n        if (isinstance(right, ast.Name) and right.id == \"Callable\" and\n                isinstance(left, ast.Constant) and left.value is None):\n            return True\n\n    return False\n\n\ndef _has_none_default(func_def: ast.FunctionDef, target_arg: ast.arg) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Check if the given arg has a default value of None.\"\"\"\n    args = func_def.args\n    # defaults apply to the last N positional args\n    all_args = args.args\n    defaults = args.defaults\n\n    if not defaults:\n        return False\n\n    # Map defaults to args (right-aligned)\n    offset = len(all_args) - len(defaults)\n    for i, arg in enumerate(all_args):\n        if arg is target_arg:\n            default_idx = i - offset\n            if 0 <= default_idx < len(defaults):\n                default = defaults[default_idx]\n                return isinstance(default, ast.Constant) and default.value is None\n    return False\n\n\ndef _find_wiring_call_sites(\n    param_name: str,\n    class_name: str,\n    trees: dict[Path, ast.Module],\n) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Search for call sites that explicitly provide the parameter by keyword.\"\"\"\n    for tree in trees.values():\n        for node in ast.walk(tree):\n            if isinstance(node, ast.Call):\n                # Check keyword arguments\n                for kw in node.keywords:\n                    if kw.arg == param_name:\n                        # Verify it's calling the right class\n                        if _is_class_call(node, class_name):\n                            return True\n    return False\n\n\ndef _is_class_call(call: ast.Call, class_name: str) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Check if a Call node is calling the specified class.\"\"\"\n    func = call.func\n    if isinstance(func, ast.Name) and func.id == class_name:\n        return True\n    if isinstance(func, ast.Attribute) and func.attr == class_name:\n        return True\n    return False\n\n\ndef analyze_unwired_callables(\n    config: WiringConfig,\n    source_dir: Path,\n) -> list[WiringFinding]:\n    \"\"\"Detect injectable callables (Optional[Callable]) that are never wired.\n\n    Algorithm (section 5.2.1):\n    1. Parse all Python files, extract Optional[Callable] constructor params\n    2. For each injectable, search all files for keyword call sites\n    3. If zero providers, emit unwired_callable finding\n    4. Apply whitelist suppression\n\n    Args:\n        config: Wiring analysis configuration.\n        source_dir: Root directory to scan.\n\n    Returns:\n        List of WiringFinding with finding_type=\"unwired_callable\".\n    \"\"\"\n    files, _ = _collect_python_files(source_dir, config.exclude_patterns)\n    trees: dict[Path, ast.Module] = {}\n\n    for f in files:\n        tree = _safe_parse(f)\n        if tree is not None:\n            trees[f] = tree\n\n    findings: list[WiringFinding] = []\n\n    for file_path, tree in trees.items():\n        injectables = _extract_injectable_params(tree, str(file_path))\n        for symbol, param_name, lineno in injectables:\n            class_name = symbol.split(\".\")[0]\n            if not _find_wiring_call_sites(param_name, class_name, trees):\n                findings.append(\n                    WiringFinding(\n                        finding_type=\"unwired_callable\",\n                        file_path=str(file_path),\n                        symbol_name=symbol,\n                        line_number=lineno,\n                        detail=(\n                            f\"Parameter '{param_name}' typed Optional[Callable] \"\n                            f\"with default None is never wired by any call site\"\n                        ),\n                        severity=\"critical\",\n                    )\n                )\n\n    # Apply whitelist\n    whitelist = load_whitelist(config.whitelist_path, config.rollout_mode)\n    return _apply_whitelist(findings, whitelist)\n\n\n# --- G-002: Orphan Module Analysis (section 5.2.2) ---\n\n\ndef _find_provider_dirs(source_dir: Path, provider_names: frozenset[str]) -> list[Path]:\n    \"\"\"Find directories matching provider_dir_names convention.\"\"\"\n    providers: list[Path] = []\n    for d in sorted(source_dir.rglob(\"*\")):\n        if d.is_dir() and d.name in provider_names:\n            providers.append(d)\n    return providers\n\n\ndef _extract_imports(tree: ast.Module) -> set[str]:\n    \"\"\"Extract all imported module/symbol names from an AST.\"\"\"\n    imports: set[str] = set()\n    for node in ast.walk(tree):\n        if isinstance(node, ast.Import):\n            for alias in node.names:\n                imports.add(alias.name)\n        elif isinstance(node, ast.ImportFrom):\n            if node.module:\n                imports.add(node.module)\n                for alias in node.names:\n                    imports.add(f\"{node.module}.{alias.name}\")\n    return imports\n\n\ndef analyze_orphan_modules(\n    config: WiringConfig,\n    source_dir: Path,\n) -> list[WiringFinding]:\n    \"\"\"Detect Python modules in provider directories with zero inbound imports.\n\n    Algorithm (section 5.2.2):\n    1. Find provider directories by config.provider_dir_names convention\n    2. For each Python file in provider dirs, check if any file outside\n       the provider dir imports it\n    3. If zero importers, emit orphan_module finding\n    4. Apply exclude_patterns and whitelist suppression\n\n    Args:\n        config: Wiring analysis configuration.\n        source_dir: Root directory to scan.\n\n    Returns:\n        List of WiringFinding with finding_type=\"orphan_module\".\n    \"\"\"\n    provider_dirs = _find_provider_dirs(source_dir, config.provider_dir_names)\n    if not provider_dirs:\n        return []\n\n    # Collect all Python files and parse them for imports\n    all_files, _ = _collect_python_files(source_dir, [])\n    all_imports: set[str] = set()\n    trees: dict[Path, ast.Module] = {}\n\n    for f in all_files:\n        tree = _safe_parse(f)\n        if tree is not None:\n            trees[f] = tree\n\n    # Gather imports from files OUTSIDE provider directories\n    for f, tree in trees.items():\n        is_in_provider = any(\n            f.resolve().is_relative_to(pd.resolve()) for pd in provider_dirs\n        )\n        if not is_in_provider:\n            all_imports.update(_extract_imports(tree))\n\n    findings: list[WiringFinding] = []\n\n    for provider_dir in provider_dirs:\n        for py_file in sorted(provider_dir.glob(\"*.py\")):\n            # Apply exclude patterns\n            if any(fnmatch(py_file.name, pat) for pat in config.exclude_patterns):\n                continue\n\n            # Derive the module path components\n            try:\n                rel = py_file.relative_to(source_dir)\n            except ValueError:\n                continue\n\n            # Build possible import names\n            module_stem = py_file.stem\n            module_dotpath = str(rel.with_suffix(\"\")).replace(\"/\", \".\").replace(\"\\\\\", \".\")\n\n            # Check if any external file imports this module\n            is_imported = False\n            for imp in all_imports:\n                if module_dotpath in imp or module_stem in imp:\n                    is_imported = True\n                    break\n\n            if not is_imported:\n                findings.append(\n                    WiringFinding(\n                        finding_type=\"orphan_module\",\n                        file_path=str(py_file),\n                        symbol_name=module_dotpath,\n                        line_number=1,\n                        detail=(\n                            f\"Module '{module_dotpath}' in provider directory \"\n                            f\"'{provider_dir.name}' has zero inbound imports\"\n                        ),\n                        severity=\"major\",\n                    )\n                )\n\n    # Apply whitelist\n    whitelist = load_whitelist(config.whitelist_path, config.rollout_mode)\n    return _apply_whitelist(findings, whitelist)\n\n\n# --- G-003: Registry Analysis (section 5.2.3) ---\n\n\ndef _matches_registry_pattern(\n    name: str, patterns: tuple[re.Pattern[str], ...]\n) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Check if a variable name matches any registry detection pattern.\"\"\"\n    return any(p.match(name) for p in patterns)\n\n\ndef _resolve_name_in_scope(\n    name: str, tree: ast.Module, all_imports: set[str]\n) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Check if a name is resolvable: defined in module or importable.\"\"\"\n    # Check module-level definitions\n    for node in ast.iter_child_nodes(tree):\n        if isinstance(node, (ast.FunctionDef, ast.AsyncFunctionDef)):\n            if node.name == name:\n                return True\n        elif isinstance(node, ast.ClassDef):\n            if node.name == name:\n                return True\n        elif isinstance(node, ast.Assign):\n            for target in node.targets:\n                if isinstance(target, ast.Name) and target.id == name:\n                    return True\n\n    # Check if importable\n    if name in all_imports:\n        return True\n\n    return False\n\n\ndef analyze_registries(\n    config: WiringConfig,\n    source_dir: Path,\n) -> list[WiringFinding]:\n    \"\"\"Detect broken dispatch registry entries referencing nonexistent callables.\n\n    Algorithm (section 5.2.3):\n    1. Scan files for module-level dict assignments matching registry patterns\n    2. For each dict entry, verify the value references an importable callable\n    3. Unresolved references emit unwired_registry findings\n\n    Args:\n        config: Wiring analysis configuration.\n        source_dir: Root directory to scan.\n\n    Returns:\n        List of WiringFinding with finding_type=\"unwired_registry\".\n    \"\"\"\n    files, _ = _collect_python_files(source_dir, config.exclude_patterns)\n    trees: dict[Path, ast.Module] = {}\n    all_imports_by_file: dict[Path, set[str]] = {}\n\n    for f in files:\n        tree = _safe_parse(f)\n        if tree is not None:\n            trees[f] = tree\n            all_imports_by_file[f] = _extract_imports(tree)\n\n    findings: list[WiringFinding] = []\n\n    for file_path, tree in trees.items():\n        file_imports = all_imports_by_file.get(file_path, set())\n\n        for node in ast.iter_child_nodes(tree):\n            if not isinstance(node, ast.Assign):\n                continue\n\n            for target in node.targets:\n                if not isinstance(target, ast.Name):\n                    continue\n                if not _matches_registry_pattern(target.id, config.registry_patterns):\n                    continue\n\n                # This is a registry assignment — check if value is a dict\n                if not isinstance(node.value, ast.Dict):\n                    continue\n\n                for key_node, val_node in zip(node.value.keys, node.value.values):\n                    if val_node is None:\n                        continue\n\n                    # Explicit None is allowed\n                    if isinstance(val_node, ast.Constant) and val_node.value is None:\n                        continue\n\n                    # Name reference — must be resolvable\n                    if isinstance(val_node, ast.Name):\n                        if not _resolve_name_in_scope(\n                            val_node.id, tree, file_imports\n                        ):\n                            key_repr = (\n                                ast.literal_eval(key_node)\n                                if isinstance(key_node, ast.Constant)\n                                else \"<dynamic>\"\n                            )\n                            findings.append(\n                                WiringFinding(\n                                    finding_type=\"unwired_registry\",\n                                    file_path=str(file_path),\n                                    symbol_name=f\"{target.id}[{key_repr!r}]\",\n                                    line_number=val_node.lineno,\n                                    detail=(\n                                        f\"Registry '{target.id}' entry \"\n                                        f\"'{key_repr}' references unresolvable \"\n                                        f\"callable '{val_node.id}'\"\n                                    ),\n                                    severity=\"critical\",\n                                )\n                            )\n\n                    # String reference — try to resolve as dotted path\n                    elif isinstance(val_node, ast.Constant) and isinstance(\n                        val_node.value, str\n                    ):\n                        ref = val_node.value\n                        parts = ref.rsplit(\".\", 1)\n                        func_name = parts[-1] if len(parts) > 1 else ref\n                        if not _resolve_name_in_scope(\n                            func_name, tree, file_imports\n                        ):\n                            key_repr = (\n                                ast.literal_eval(key_node)\n                                if isinstance(key_node, ast.Constant)\n                                else \"<dynamic>\"\n                            )\n                            findings.append(\n                                WiringFinding(\n                                    finding_type=\"unwired_registry\",\n                                    file_path=str(file_path),\n                                    symbol_name=f\"{target.id}[{key_repr!r}]\",\n                                    line_number=val_node.lineno,\n                                    detail=(\n                                        f\"Registry '{target.id}' entry \"\n                                        f\"'{key_repr}' references unresolvable \"\n                                        f\"string path '{ref}'\"\n                                    ),\n                                    severity=\"critical\",\n                                )\n                            )\n\n    # Apply whitelist\n    whitelist = load_whitelist(config.whitelist_path, config.rollout_mode)\n    return _apply_whitelist(findings, whitelist)\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Top-level entry point\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n\ndef run_wiring_analysis(\n    config: WiringConfig,\n    source_dir: Path,\n) -> WiringReport:\n    \"\"\"Run all three wiring analyzers and produce a WiringReport.\n\n    Args:\n        config: Wiring analysis configuration.\n        source_dir: Root directory to scan.\n\n    Returns:\n        WiringReport aggregating findings from all analyzers.\n    \"\"\"\n    start = time.monotonic()\n\n    _, skipped = _collect_python_files(source_dir, config.exclude_patterns)\n    files, _ = _collect_python_files(source_dir, config.exclude_patterns)\n    files_analyzed = len(files)\n\n    unwired = analyze_unwired_callables(config, source_dir)\n    orphans = analyze_orphan_modules(config, source_dir)\n    registries = analyze_registries(config, source_dir)\n\n    duration = time.monotonic() - start\n\n    return WiringReport(\n        target_dir=str(source_dir),\n        files_analyzed=files_analyzed,\n        files_skipped=skipped,\n        unwired_callables=unwired,\n        orphan_modules=orphans,\n        unwired_registries=registries,\n        scan_duration_seconds=round(duration, 4),\n        rollout_mode=config.rollout_mode,\n    )\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
